Done:

(middlewares)
1.auth middleware - gets token and gets user in req.auth.user or req.auth.partner as required. Also sets req.auth.type.admin/superadmin to true or false
2.authOnly middleware – checks if any kind of user/partner is present
3.isAdmin middleware – checks if req.auth.type.admin/superadmin is true and only allows admins/superadmins to proceed
4.isSuperAdmin – only allows super admins to proceed 

(models)
1.Partner – only for the health partners
2.User- for users/admins/superadmins

(routes)
user
1.userregister- register for users only not for admins/superadmins. While registering the admin and superadmin property is set to false
2.userlogin – login for admins/superadmins/user

healthp
1.addhealthp – adds hp done by admin
2.loginhp – login for hp

sadmin
1.addadmin – sa can add admin
2.deleteadmin – sa can delete admin

09/02/2023, 08:55 - Aditya Tsec: //Update course progress
router.get("/updatecourseprogress", isUser, async (req, res) => {
	const userId=req.auth.user._id;
	const courseId=req.body.courseId;
	const link=req.body.link;
	const foundUser=await User.findOne({_id:userId});
	var courseprogress=foundUser.courseprogress;
	var len=courseprogress.length;
	for (let i = 0; i < len; i++) {
		if (courseprogress[i].courseId === courseId) {
			courseprogress[i].watchedlinks.push(link);
			break;
  		}
	}
	const updatedUser = await User.findByIdAndUpdate(
		userId,
		{ courseprogress: courseprogress },{new:true}
	);

	res.json(updatedUser);



});

22/07/2023, 13:52 - Aditya Tsec: def get_user_posts():
    posts_data = []
    links_data = []
    mentions_data = []

    # Get dids of 5 users
    repos = users[:1]

    for user in repos:
        did = user['did']
        cursor = None  # Initialize cursor as None

        while True:
            # Construct URL with did and cursor
            url = f"https://bsky.social/xrpc/com.atproto.repo.listRecords?collection=app.bsky.feed.post&repo={did}"
            if cursor:
                url += f"&cursor={cursor}"

            # Make GET request
            response = requests.get(url)
            data = response.json()

            # Extract records from response data
            records = data.get('records', [])

            # Iterate over records
            for record in records:
                cid = record['cid']
                uri = record['uri']
                text = record['value'].get('text', '')
                createdAt = record['value']['createdAt']
                date, time = createdAt.split("T")

                # Extract did from the uri
                did_from_uri = uri.split('/')[2]  # Assuming the uri format is fixed as shown in the example

                reply = record['value'].get('reply', {})
                rootcid = reply.get('root', {}).get('cid', '')
                rooturi = reply.get('root', {}).get('uri', '')
                parentcid = reply.get('parent', {}).get('cid', '')
                parenturi = reply.get('parent', {}).get('uri', '')

                post_info = {
                    "cid": cid,
                    "uri": uri,
                    "did": did_from_uri,  # Add the 'did' column here
                    "text": text,
                    "rootcid": rootcid,
                    "rooturi": rooturi,
                    "parentcid": parentcid,
                    "parenturi": parenturi,
                    "date": date,
                    "time": time
                }

                posts_data.append(post_info)
                
                facets = record['value'].get('facets', [])
                if facets:
                    for facet in facets:
                        features = facet.get('features', [])
                        for feature in features:
                            if feature.get('$type') == 'app.bsky.richtext.facet#link':
                                link = feature.get('uri', '')
                                link_info = {
                                    "did": did,
                                    "cid": cid,
                                    "uri": uri,
                                    "link": link
                                }
                                links_data.append(link_info)

                            if feature.get('$type') == 'app.bsky.richtext.facet#mention':
                                mention = feature.get('did', '')
                                mention_info = {
                                    "did": did,
                                    "cid": cid,
                                    "uri": uri,
                                    "mention": mention
                                }
                                mentions_data.append(mention_info)

            # Check if cursor is available
            if 'cursor' not in data:
                break

            # Update cursor
            cursor = data['cursor']

    posts_df = pd.DataFrame(posts_data)
    links_df = pd.DataFrame(links_data)
    mentions_df = pd.DataFrame(mentions_data)
    return posts_df, links_df, mentions_df

# Example usage
posts_df, links_df, mentions_df = get_user_posts()

print("POSTS:")
print(len(posts_df))
print(posts_df.head())
print("----------------------------------------------------")
print("LINKS:")
print(len(links_df))
print(links_df.head())
print("----------------------------------------------------")
print("MENTIONS:")
print(len(mentions_df))
print(mentions_df.head())

Content Moderation Challenges: Insights into the complexities of content moderation, including the delicate balance between personalization and safety, handling controversial topics, and ensuring proactive moderation.
Role of AI in Content Moderation: A comprehensive overview of how AI and machine learning technologies contribute to detecting inappropriate content, managing user-generated content, and maintaining a safe environment for users.
Statistics and Transparency: Statistics from reputable sources, such as Pew Research Center, and insights from Snapchat's transparency reports, providing quantitative context to the paper's narrative.
Questions for Further Discussion: A set of thoughtful questions to initiate a deeper conversation about Snapchat's content moderation practices, the role of AI, collaboration with external entities, and the platform's approach to context-dependent content
